      <p>Laws regarding <a href="/wiki/Incest" title="Incest">incest</a> (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Human_sexual_activity" title="Human sexual activity">sexual activity</a> between family members or close relatives) vary considerably between jurisdictions, and depend on the type of sexual activity and the nature of the family relationship of the parties involved, as well as the age and sex of the parties. Besides legal prohibitions, at least some forms of <a href="/wiki/Incest" title="Incest">incest</a> are also socially taboo or frowned upon in most cultures around the world. </p>
      <p>Incest laws may involve restrictions on <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">marriage</a> rights, which also vary between jurisdictions. When incest involves an adult and a child, it is considered to be a form of <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">child sexual abuse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Levesque_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levesque-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNchildren_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNchildren-2">[2]</a></sup> When it is between two consenting adults, it is sometimes called consanguinamory.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Degrees_of_relationship">Degrees of relationship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Degrees of relationship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coefficient_of_relationship" title="Coefficient of relationship">Coefficient of relationship</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Laws regarding incest are sometimes expressed in terms of degrees of relationship. The degree of relationship is calculated by counting the number of generations back to a common ancestor. Consanguinity (but not affinity) relationships may be summarized as follows: </p> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Degree of <br>relationship</th> 
         <th>Relationship</th> 
         <th>Average DNA<br>shared&nbsp;% </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td></td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Inbred_strain" title="Inbred strain">Inbred strain</a></td> 
         <td>99% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>0</td> 
         <td>identical twins; clones</td> 
         <td>100%<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1</td> 
         <td>parent-offspring<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></td> 
         <td>50% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1</td> 
         <td>full siblings</td> 
         <td>50% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>2</td> 
         <td>3/4-siblings or sibling-cousins</td> 
         <td>37.5% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>2</td> 
         <td>grandparent-grandchild</td> 
         <td>25% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>2</td> 
         <td>half-siblings</td> 
         <td>25% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>2</td> 
         <td>aunt/uncle-nephew/niece</td> 
         <td>25% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>2</td> 
         <td>double first cousins</td> 
         <td>25% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>3</td> 
         <td>great grandparent-great grandchild</td> 
         <td>12.5% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>3</td> 
         <td>first cousins</td> 
         <td>12.5% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>3</td> 
         <td>quadruple second cousins</td> 
         <td>12.5% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>4</td> 
         <td>triple second cousins</td> 
         <td>9.38% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>4</td> 
         <td>half-first cousins</td> 
         <td>6.25% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>4</td> 
         <td>first cousins once removed</td> 
         <td>6.25% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>4</td> 
         <td>double second cousins</td> 
         <td>6.25% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>5</td> 
         <td>second cousins</td> 
         <td>3.13% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>7</td> 
         <td>third cousins</td> 
         <td>0.78% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>9</td> 
         <td>fourth cousins</td> 
         <td>0.20%<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Most laws regarding <a href="/wiki/Prohibited_degree_of_kinship" title="Prohibited degree of kinship">prohibited degree of kinship</a> concern relations of <i>r</i> = 25% or higher, while most permit unions of individuals with <i>r</i> = 12.5% or lower. In 24 <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">states</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cousin_marriage" title="Cousin marriage">cousin marriages</a> are prohibited. Also, most laws make no provision for the rare case of marriage between double first cousins. Incest laws may also include prohibitions of unions between biologically unrelated individuals if there is a close legal relationship, such as <a href="/wiki/Adoption" title="Adoption">adoption</a> or step relations. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Laws_regarding_incest_between_consenting_adults">Laws regarding incest between consenting adults</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Laws regarding incest between consenting adults">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:817px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Incest_legislation.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Incest_legislation.svg/815px-Incest_legislation.svg.png" decoding="async" width="815" height="413" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Incest_legislation.svg/1223px-Incest_legislation.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Incest_legislation.svg/1630px-Incest_legislation.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="856" data-file-height="434"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Incest_legislation.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div><b>Incest between consenting adults by country:</b> 
          <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
          <div class="legend">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span id="C.C3.B4te_d.27Ivoire_.28Ivory_Coast.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Côte_d'Ivoire_(Ivory_Coast)">Côte d'Ivoire (Ivory Coast)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Côte d'Ivoire (Ivory Coast)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Consensual incest between adults is legal in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" class="mw-redirect" title="Côte d'Ivoire">Côte d'Ivoire</a> (Ivory Coast).<sup id="cite_ref-MPICC_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MPICC-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, since 2007, incest is the <a href="/wiki/Sexual_penetration" title="Sexual penetration">sexual penetration</a> between persons who are related as follows: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>lineally, that is, if one person is a direct descendant of the other.</li> 
       <li>within the first degree of <a href="/wiki/Consanguinuity" class="mw-redirect" title="Consanguinuity">consanguinuity</a>, that is, where one person is a direct descendant of a parent of the other; this category includes siblings as well as an uncle or aunt with a niece or nephew.</li> 
       <li>within the first degree of <a href="/wiki/Affinity_(law)" title="Affinity (law)">affinity</a>, that is, where one person is the direct ancestor or descendant of the spouse of the other person.</li> 
       <li>as adoptive parent and adopted child.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Before 2007, incest was a <a href="/wiki/Common_law_offence" title="Common law offence">common law offence</a> which extended to the same degrees of relationship but which applied only to vaginal intercourse.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Zimbabwe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Zimbabwe, most forms of incest are illegal and an offender is currently liable to a fine up to or exceeding level fourteen (about US$5000) or imprisonment for a period not exceeding five years or both.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Incest is classified as "sexual intercourse within a prohibited degree of relationship".<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> A prohibited degree of relationship would be that of a parent and his or her natural or adoptive child, a step-parent and his or her step-child, whether the step-child's parent and step-parent are married under the Marriage Act [Chapter 5:11] or the Customary Marriages Act [Chapter 5:07], or are parties to an unregistered customary law marriage, and whether or not the child was over the age of eighteen years at the time of the marriage; a brother and sister, whether of whole or half blood; or an uncle and his niece; or a grand-uncle and his grand-niece; or an aunt and her nephew; or a grand-aunt and her grand-nephew; or a grandparent and his or her grandchild and any person and his or her first or second cousin. In cases of first and second cousins an individual charged with such a crime can raise a defense that the cultural or religious customs or traditions of the community to which he or she belongs do not prohibit marriage between first or second cousins; or in the case of a person who is a member of a community governed by customary law, that the cultural or religious customs or traditions of the particular community to which he or she belongs do not prohibit marriage between first or second cousins. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas">Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Argentina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, incest is legal if both individuals are over the <a href="/wiki/Ages_of_consent_in_South_America#Argentina" title="Ages of consent in South America">minimum age of consent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Marriage between third-degree relatives and beyond is allowed, with the exception of marriage involving lineal ancestors and descendants, which is considered null and void disregarding the degree of separation (parent/offspring, grandparent-grandchild).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Brazil has no criminal punishment if the involved are over the age of 14 (the clear <a href="/wiki/Age_of_consent_in_Brazil" title="Age of consent in Brazil">age of consent</a> in force; before 2011, though, sex with people as young as 12 and as elder as 17 was in a legal grey area, with legal guardian-reported sex with those aged 12 and 13 being prosecuted as statutory rape, but unlike as with those aged 11 and younger not directly prosecuted by the State without a report by either the legal guardians or the adolescents themselves—unlike now, where the police forces prosecute all statutory rape-related cases without distinction—, and legal guardian-reported sex with those aged 14, 15, 16 and 17 being prosecuted as corruption of minors, but prosecution as corruption of minors for non-commercial consented sexual activity between people out of a defined hierarchy fell), capable of acting upon their legal rights, and that consent means that the relationship is absent of any kind of coercion or fraud.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cousin_marriage" title="Cousin marriage">First cousin marriages</a>, once fairly common in some regions in the 19th century, are allowed on demand as all other marriages, while <a href="/wiki/Avunculate_marriage" title="Avunculate marriage">avunculate ones</a> (those between uncles or aunts and nephews or nieces), the preferred by some Amazonian Amerindian tribes, and those between half-siblings, are allowed provided that those contracting it have a health check.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-direito_mais_direito_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-direito_mais_direito-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-direitobrasil_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-direitobrasil-36">[36]</a></sup> Marriages between parents and their children (both consanguineous and adoptive) or between siblings (both consanguineous and adoptive) are invalid, but, as stated above, non-rape sexual relationships between persons older than the age of consent are likely otherwise treated legally as all others, irrespectively of consanguinity (information over the possibility or validity of <i lang="pt" title="Portuguese language text">uniões estáveis</i> in such situations are nevertheless unclear or unexistent, but since those in these relationships are already consanguineous and thus inherently inside a legal family entity, the rights offered by such unions—recognizing a family entity between unrelated single persons—are most likely pointless, with the exceptional cases being only the remote possibility of people who were adopted contracting a relationship with a biological close family member). </p>
      <p>Brazilian law, by the Article 1521 of the Civil Code, also extends the invalidity of marriage between parents and children to grandparents and grandchildren or any other sort of ascendant-descendant relationship (both consanguineous and adoptive), parents-in-law and children-in-law even after the divorce of the earlier couple (see <a href="/wiki/Affinity_(law)" title="Affinity (law)">affinity</a>), as well as to stepparents and stepchildren, and former husbands or wives to an adoptive parent who did this unilaterally (regarded as an equivalent, in families formed by adoption, to stepparents and stepchildren); and extends the invalidity of marriage between siblings to biological cousin-siblings.<sup id="cite_ref-direito_mais_direito_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-direito_mais_direito-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-direitobrasil_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-direitobrasil-36">[36]</a></sup> It also formerly prohibited the avunculate marriages and extended the prohibition for marriage between siblings to half-siblings, both cited above, but the Decrete Law 3.200/1941 made marriage possible for those non-ascended/descended in consanguinity of third degree (25%) provided both have health checks.<sup id="cite_ref-direito_mais_direito_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-direito_mais_direito-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-direitobrasil_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-direitobrasil-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brazilian law never held marriages between double first cousins as a reason for invalidity, even though those have a consanguinity <a href="/wiki/Coefficient_of_relationship#Human_genealogy" title="Coefficient of relationship">as strong as that of half-siblings</a>, and those, as other first cousins, are not asked health checks to marry, doing so in the same way as non-related people. Also legally treated much like non-related people are stepsiblings, while those who are stepsiblings and half-siblings (that is, those who have a half-sibling who is also child of a latter married spouse of one's parent) are treated like half-siblings who are not stepsiblings, being demanded health checks before marrying. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Under Canadian federal law, incest is defined as having a sexual relationship with a sibling (including half-sibling), child/parent or grandchild/grandparent, requiring knowledge of the existence of the blood relationship. It is punishable by up to 14 years' imprisonment, and a person who commits incest with someone under the age of 16 is liable to a minimum imprisonment of five years.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Chile, incest between lineal ancestors and descendants and between full siblings is prohibited. It is punishable by up to 1 year in prison.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Mexico, The crime of incest when the ancestors have sexual relations with their descendants will be punished with a sentence of one to six years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-Gobierno_de_México_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gobierno_de_México-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Laws_regarding_incest_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws regarding incest in the United States">Laws regarding incest in the United States</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Prohibited_degree_of_kinship#United_States" title="Prohibited degree of kinship">Prohibited degree of kinship §&nbsp;United States</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Laws regarding incest in the United States vary widely among jurisdictions regarding both the definition of the offense and penalties for its commission. The <a href="/wiki/Legality_of_incest_in_the_United_States" title="Legality of incest in the United States">laws regarding incest in the United States</a> article summarizes these laws for individual U.S. states and the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" class="mw-redirect" title="District of Columbia">District of Columbia</a>. </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the District of Columbia and every state and inhabited territory have some form of codified incest prohibition. In most states, sexual activity between a lineal ancestor and a lineal descendant (parent, grandparent with child or grandchild), siblings (brother-sister) and aunt-nephew, uncle-niece is penalized as incest. However, individual statutes vary widely. <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a> has repealed its criminal incest statute,<sup id="cite_ref-harv001_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harv001-39">[39]</a></sup> and only criminalizes incestuous marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-NDAA_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NDAA-40">[40]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> "targets only parental figures",<sup id="cite_ref-harv001_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harv001-39">[39]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> does not apply any penalties when both parties are 12 years of age or older.<sup id="cite_ref-MPICC_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MPICC-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-harv001_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harv001-39">[39]</a></sup> The most severe penalties for incest are in <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, which punishes incest with up to 20 years in prison, Georgia where a penalty for incest is up to 30 years in prison, Wisconsin where the penalty for incest is up to 40 years in prison, and in the states of <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">Idaho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a> where a penalty of up to life imprisonment for incest may be given. </p>
      <p>In some states, sex between first cousins is prohibited (see <a href="/wiki/Cousin_marriage_law_in_the_United_States_by_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Cousin marriage law in the United States by state">cousin marriage law in the United States by state</a> for cousin sex, as well as cousin marriage, being outlawed in some states). Many states also apply incest laws to non-blood relations, including stepparents, stepsiblings, in-laws and people related through adoption.<sup id="cite_ref-Turner_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turner-41">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainland">Mainland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Mainland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The People's Republic of <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> prohibits two kinds of marriages in terms of kinship.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ol>
       <li>One person is the direct descendant of another.</li> 
       <li>One person is another's first cousin.</li>
      </ol> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hong_Kong">Hong Kong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hong Kong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Hong Kong, it is illegal to have sexual intercourse with certain close relatives, even if they are consenting adults. The prohibited relationships are grandfather-granddaughter, father-daughter, brother-sister and mother-son. Punishment is up to 20 years' imprisonment for male offenders and up to 14 years' imprisonment for female offenders.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The law does not cover sexual intercourse with more distant relatives, such as an aunt, uncle, niece, nephew and cousin. It only addresses male-on-female and female-on-male sexual intercourse, and it appears that consensual same-sex incest is not illegal. The law makes an assumption that a female below the age of 16 has no ability to consent to sexual intercourse, therefore a female below 16 cannot commit incest. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Macau">Macau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Macau">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>According to Macau's civil code, people in direct line kinship or in the second degree of collateral kinship cannot marry each other.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Indian_Penal_Code" title="Indian Penal Code">Indian Penal Code</a> (IPC) does not contain any specific provision against incest and also there is no law to support incest relationships, but there are general provisions relating to <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse_of_children" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual abuse of children">sexual abuse of children</a> by their custodian, such as a parent or teacher.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> More over the rule of kinship or marriage is governed by the different marriage laws.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Consensual incest between adults is legal in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, it is incest to have sexual intercourse with a person who under the law, religion, custom or usage that applies to the person he or she is not permitted to marry on account of their relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition to whipping, persons convicted of incest face a minimum sentence of 6 years' imprisonment and a maximum sentence of 20 years' imprisonment. It is a defense against the charge if the person did not know the relationship was not permitted or if the sexual intercourse was done without his or her consent. Girls below the age of 16 and boys below the age of 13 are deemed to be incapable of giving consent. (The age of consent for sex in Malaysia is 16 for both sexes.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>) </p>
      <p>While it is unclear to which family members the incest law applies, a verdict from the High Court in Sabah and Sarawak in 2011 provided some indication about the sentencing guidelines. It described incest as a "heinous crime" but that the degree of kinship between the parties dictates the "level of repulsion" which the court translates into a sentence imposed. The verdict said the worst on such a scale is incest committed by a father to his biological daughter or a brother to his biological sister, and that such offenders should receive the harshest sentence. It said an uncle and his maternal niece committing incest is not on that same level and, if there was no violence involved, the length of the sentence should reflect it.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are more severe sentences for those who commit incest through rape. The offence of incestuous rape is punishable with not less than 8 years' imprisonment and not more than 30 years' imprisonment. In addition, those convicted receive not less than 10 strokes.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Malaysian law also considers sexual intercourse with the stepfamily to be incestuous.<sup id="cite_ref-NST2012_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NST2012-52">[52]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The legal code of Pakistan defines incest as marriage (<a href="/wiki/Copulation" class="mw-redirect" title="Copulation">consortion</a>) between a male and either his: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>wife or former wife of father, grandfather and further ancestors</li> 
       <li>Mother, grandmother and further ancestors</li> 
       <li>Daughter, granddaughter and further descendants</li> 
       <li>full or half-sister</li> 
       <li>parents' sisters, grandparents' sisters and further ancestors' sisters</li> 
       <li>daughter, granddaughter and further descendant of full or half-sibling</li> 
       <li>suckling ancestor</li> 
       <li>suckling sister</li> 
       <li>Mother, grandmother and further ancestors of wife or former wife</li> 
       <li>Daughter, granddaughter of wife or former wife</li> 
       <li>Wife or former wife of true son or grandson and further descendants</li> 
       <li>Sororal <a href="/wiki/Polygyny" title="Polygyny">polygyny</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Both participants are guilty if they commit the above acts and are charged with <a href="/wiki/Zina" title="Zina">zina</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="uncited claims (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Article 81 of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Code_of_the_Philippines" title="Civil Code of the Philippines">Civil Code of the Philippines</a> considers marriages between the following incestuous and void from their performance:<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ol>
       <li>Between brothers and sisters, whether of the full or half blood;</li> 
       <li>Between collateral relatives by blood within the fourth civil degree</li>
      </ol> 
      <p>A similar prohibition can be found in Articles 37 and 38 of the <a href="/wiki/Family_Code_of_the_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="Family Code of the Philippines">Family Code</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 1973 visa proceedings case of <i>In re: Bautista</i>, an Immigration Officer denied entry to a married couple who were second cousins. In reaching the decision, the immigration officer relied on subsection 1 of Article 81 of the Civil Code. However, on appeal, it was found that the parties were collateral relatives and therefore fell under subsection 2 of the same Code, which prohibits marriages between relatives by blood within the fourth civil degree. The fourth civil degree includes first cousins. Second cousins, who are the children of first cousins, fall under the fifth civil degree and are not covered by the prohibition. The marriage, being valid under the laws of the place of celebration, was then recognized for immigration purposes only.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.officialgazette.gov.ph/1977/02/04/presidential-decree-no-1083-s-1977-2/">Code of Muslim Personal Laws of the Philippines</a> prohibit by consanguinity (<i>tahrimjbin-nasab</i>) the following marriages:<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ol>
       <li>Ascendants and descendants of any degree;</li> 
       <li>Brothers and sisters, whether germane, consanguine or uterine; and</li> 
       <li>Brothers or sisters and their descendants within the third civil degree.</li>
      </ol> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Section 376G of the Penal Code specifies that "a male, of or above the age of 16, having sexual relations with his grand-daughter, daughter, sister, half-sister, mother or grandmother, with or without consent, shall be guilty of an offence. Any woman of or above the age of 16 years who, with consent, permits her grandfather, father, brother, half-brother, son or grandson (whether such relationship is or is not traced through lawful wedlock) to penetrate her in the manner described in subsection (1)(a) or (b), knowing him to be her grandfather, father, brother, half-brother, son or grandson, as the case may be, shall be guilty of an offence."<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan">Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, officially the Republic of China (ROC), Article 983 of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://law.moj.gov.tw/Eng/LawClass/LawContent.aspx?PCODE=B0000001">Civil Code</a> prohibits marrying any lineal relative by blood or by marriage, collateral relative by blood if it is within the sixth degree of relationship (except relative by adoption who is of the same rank), or if collateral relative by marriage is within the fifth degree of relationship of a different rank. Relatives by marriage or adoption are prohibited marriage and cannot marry even after the marriage or adoption has ended. The degree of relationship is calculated vertically, therefore a sibling is within the second degree of relationship. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.judicial.gov.tw/constitutionalcourt/p03.asp">Judicial Yuan Interpretation</a> No.32 and No. 91 allows marriage between siblings by adoption when the adoption was intended for the marriage. When the interpretation was made, it was not uncommon for parents to adopt a child so that their own child can marry the adopted child when both children have grown up. Article 230 of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://law.moj.gov.tw/LawClass/LawContent.aspx?PCODE=C0000001">Penal Code</a> prohibits sexual intercourse between any lineal relatives by blood or collateral relatives within the third degree of relationship by blood. Violators may be imprisoned for up to 5 years. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thailand">Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Incestuous relations between persons (over 15 years old) are not prohibited by law. Incestuous marriage is prohibited by law.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sibling_marriage" class="mw-redirect" title="Sibling marriage">Sibling marriage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avunculate_marriage" title="Avunculate marriage">avunculate marriage</a> is prohibited, while <a href="/wiki/Cousin_marriage" title="Cousin marriage">cousin marriage</a> is legal.<sup id="cite_ref-Turkishcivil_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turkishcivil-58">[58]</a></sup> Marriage between parents and offspring is also prohibited, even when there is no blood relationship, i.e. <a href="/wiki/Adoptive_parent" class="mw-redirect" title="Adoptive parent">adoptive parent</a> or <a href="/wiki/Parent-in-law" title="Parent-in-law">parent-in-law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Turkishcivil_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turkishcivil-58">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam">Vietnam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Vietnam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Incest between people of direct blood line is illegal in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and is punishable by sentencing to between 6 months and 5 years of imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-Penal_Code_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penal_Code-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Most European countries prohibit incest;<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> apart from those listed below, these include: (all articles refer to the Penal Codes) Albania Article 106,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Ukraine Article 155 Paragraph 2,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Slovenia Article 195,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Slovakia Section 203,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Serbia Article 197,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Poland Article 201,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Norway Article 197 and 198,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Bosnia and Herzegovina Article 201,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Hungary Article 199,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Bulgaria Article 154,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> and Cyprus Article 147.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Countries that allow incest between consenting adult siblings include France, Spain, the <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a> and Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-focus-2011-05-22_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-focus-2011-05-22-72">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Austria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, incest between lineal ancestors and descendants and between full siblings is prohibited. It is punishable by up to 3 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Czech_Republic">Czech Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Czech Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Section 188 of the Czech Criminal code<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> prohibits incest between lineal ancestors and descendants and siblings. The maximum penalty is 3 years of imprisonment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, incest is sex between lineal ancestors and descendants and between full siblings. Sex with a descendant is punishable by up to 6 years imprisonment. Sex between siblings is punishable by up to 2 years imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Estonia">Estonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Estonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, sexual intercourse or commission of another act of sexual nature by a parent, person holding parental rights or grandparent with a child or grandchild is punishable by 2 to 8 years imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland">Finland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Finland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, sexual acts between one's full sibling (but not half-sibling), ancestor or descendant are punishable by a fine or up to two years in prison for "sexual act between close relatives". However, no punishment is given to a person who was under 18 years old when performing a sexual act with a parent or grandparent or if the person was forced or illegally persuaded to perform the sexual act.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The marriage law defines, that marriage between one's sibling, half-sibling, ancestor or descendant is forbidden.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="France.2C_Belgium.2C_and_Luxembourg"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="France,_Belgium,_and_Luxembourg">France, Belgium, and Luxembourg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: France, Belgium, and Luxembourg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The 1810 <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Code" title="Napoleonic Code">penal code</a>, which was promulgated by <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> I and adopted throughout most of Europe, abolished incest laws in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-34">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>. On 27 January 2010, France reinstated laws against incest. The new law, however, defines incest as rape or sexual abuse on a minor "by a relative or any other person having lawful or de facto authority over the victim".<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Incest between consenting adults is not prohibited. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, incest is legally defined as vaginal intercourse between lineal ancestors and descendants (parents, grandparents, great-grandparents and their children, grandchildren, great-grandchildren) and between full and half-siblings.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The penalty is a fine or up to 3 years of prison. Incest between relatives who are minors (below 18 years old) at the time of offence is not punishable but remains a crime, therefore aiding and abetting of incest between related minors is punishable.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Regarding marriage, the same rules apply and prohibit marriage between aforementioned relatives.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The criminal liability of incest among consenting adults is disputed in Germany. In the case of <a href="/wiki/Patrick_St%C3%BCbing" title="Patrick Stübing">Patrick Stübing</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Constitutional_Court" title="Federal Constitutional Court">Federal Constitutional Court</a> ruled in 2008 that the criminalization of incest is constitutional in a 7:1 vote with one judge dissenting.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2014 the <a href="/wiki/German_Ethics_Council" title="German Ethics Council">German Ethics Council</a> recommended that the government abolish laws criminalizing consensual incest between adult siblings, arguing that such bans impinge upon citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Article 345<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> of the Greek Penal Code as modified by Article 2, Paragraph 8 of Law 3625/2007<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and Article 3 Paragraph 10 of Law 3727/2008<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> prohibits incestuous relations between relatives of both ascending and descending line, and between half or full siblings, and imposes (1) for the ascending relative (for example father, uncle, grandfather etc.): at least 10 years' imprisonment if the descending relative is under 15 years old, imprisonment if 15 but not 18 years old, and maximum 2 years' imprisonment if 18 years and older; (2) for the descending relative (for example child, nephew etc.) maximum 2 years' imprisonment; (3) for half- or full siblings maximum 2 years' imprisonment. Paragraph 2 of Article 345 Penal Code also states that if the descending relative and the half or full siblings were under 18 years old, they might be cleared of any charge. </p>
      <p>Also, Article 1357<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> of the Greek Civil Code prohibits the marriage of relatives of direct blood line in totality, and up the four degrees of <a href="/wiki/Consanguinity" title="Consanguinity">consanguinity</a> of the secondary blood line (for example you can marry the first cousin of your mother / father, but not your first cousin). Article 1358 of the Greek Civil Code also prohibits the marriage of relatives in law totally in direct blood line, and up the third degree of the secondary blood line. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iceland">Iceland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Iceland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Article 200<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> of the Icelandic Penal Code prohibits incestuous relations between relatives of both ascending and descending line, and between half or full siblings, and (1) imposes for the ascending relative (for example father, uncle, grandfather etc.): imprisonment up to a maximum of 12 years if the descending relative is between 15 and 17 years old, imprisonment up to a maximum of 8 years if 18 years and older; (2) for siblings a maximum 4 years' imprisonment—if the half or full siblings were under 18 years old, they might be cleared of any charge. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_Ireland">Republic of Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Republic of Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Incest is illegal in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> under the Punishment of Incest Act 1908,<sup id="cite_ref-Incest_Act_1908_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Incest_Act_1908-91">[91]</a></sup> which pre-dates the foundation of the state. </p>
      <p>It is illegal for a male to have sexual intercourse with his granddaughter, mother, daughter, sister, or half-sister; and for a female (over sixteen years of age) with her grandfather, father, son, brother, or half-brother. The act does not refer to other familial relationships (such as grandson-grandmother), or <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">same-sex relations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Incest_Act_1908_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Incest_Act_1908-91">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prior to the amendment of the 1908 Act in 2019, incest was punishable by up to 7 years' imprisonment for a female and up to life imprisonment for a male. The Criminal Law (Sexual Offences) (Amendment) Act 2019 amended the Act of 1908 to provide for a maximum term of 10 years' imprisonment for both males and females.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Occasionally, offenders convicted of incest will be admitted to a <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_hospital" title="Psychiatric hospital">psychiatric hospital</a> for psychiatric treatment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Incest is illegal in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> only if it provokes public scandal, according to Article 564 of the Penal code and punishable from 2 to 8 years' imprisonment, open to more years for the older person if the other was under aged.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latvia">Latvia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Latvia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Incest is not criminally prohibited in Latvia except as part of the general protection of adolescents from sexual abuse.<sup id="cite_ref-eurocommunicator.ge_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurocommunicator.ge-95">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lithuania">Lithuania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Lithuania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Criminal Code of Lithuania does not explicitly foresee a criminal punishment for incest between adults, however it does state that "A father, mother, guardian, custodian or another lawful representative of a child or a person holding statutory powers in respect of a minor who has sexual intercourse or otherwise satisfied his sexual desires with that minor, in the absence of characteristics of a rape, sexual assault or sexual abuse, shall be punished by a fine or by restriction of liberty or by arrest or by a custodial sentence for a term of up to six years." Thereby, the law explicitly foresees a criminal punishment for incest between a parent and a child or for persons of similar standing.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Consensual incest between adults is legal in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MPICC_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MPICC-27">[27]</a></sup> Marriage is forbidden between ancestors and descendants or between siblings, although the Minister of Justice may grant dispensation in the case of siblings by adoption. Marriage is also forbidden between blood relations of the third and fourth degree, unless both partners have signed a declaration of consent. (Dutch civil law book 1, articles 41 and 42.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>) </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norway">Norway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Norway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Incest is illegal in <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> and is defined as intercourse between ancestors and descendants, siblings, and even stepfamily. It is punishable by up to 5 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, incest is defined in Article 201 of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080309141745/http://isip.sejm.gov.pl/servlet/Search?todo=open&amp;id=WDU19970880553">Penal Code</a> as sexual intercourse with an ancestor, descendant, guardian, ward, brother, or sister, and is punishable by imprisonment for no less than 3 months and no more than 5 years. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portugal">Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Incest is not specifically prohibited under Portuguese law.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Incest is defined in the <a href="/wiki/Penal_Code_of_Romania" title="Penal Code of Romania">Penal Code</a> as "consensual sexual relations between lineal relatives or between siblings" and is punished by a year to 5 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, consensual sex between adults, including incest, is not a crime.<sup id="cite_ref-MPICC_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MPICC-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> However, under the <a href="/wiki/Family_Code_of_Russia" title="Family Code of Russia">Family Code of Russia</a>, persons who are related lineally, siblings, half-siblings, and a stepparent and a stepchild may not marry.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovenia">Slovenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Slovenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Incest in <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> is not criminally prohibited unless one person is a <a href="/wiki/Minor_(law)" title="Minor (law)">minor</a>. A person who has sexual relations with a blood relation minor is punished to 2 years in prison.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Consensual incest between adults is legal in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MPICC_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MPICC-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Incest with a descendant or a full sibling is prohibited by law in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-swed001_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swed001-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Half-siblings can marry, but require special approval by the government. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Article 213 of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Swiss_Penal_Code&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Swiss Penal Code (page does not exist)">Swiss Penal Code</a> prohibits incest. Intercourse among siblings or other persons related by blood in direct line is punishable by up to 3 years' imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The federal government proposed to abolish this prohibition in 2010, arguing that in the few cases where persons were convicted of incest (three since 1984), other sexual crimes such as child sexual abuse were also committed.<sup id="cite_ref-Le_Temps_2010_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Le_Temps_2010-106">[106]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sexual_offences_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Sexual offences in the United Kingdom">Sexual offences in the United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prohibited_degree_of_kinship#United_Kingdom" title="Prohibited degree of kinship">Prohibited degree of kinship §&nbsp;United Kingdom</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Legislation regarding sexual offences in the United Kingdom is <a href="/wiki/Devolved" class="mw-redirect" title="Devolved">devolved</a>. Sex with an adult who is related as parent, adoptive parent, grandparent, child, adopted child, grandchild, brother, sister, half-brother, half-sister, uncle, aunt, nephew or niece, is illegal. In England and Wales the offence is against the Sexual Offences Act 2003<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> which effectively replaced the offence of incest with two new wider groups of offences: familial child sex offences (sections 25–29) and sex with an adult relative (sections 64–65). The punishment for sex between adults knowingly related in the aforementioned ways via penetration is liabile to a maximum imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> While sexual activity with a child family member can incur imprisonment for a term not exceeding 14 years.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> These laws are intended to protect the rights of people, so as to avoid potential violation. However, these laws still outlaw consensual sexual relationships between family members, even if they are fully willing and knowledgeable of the potential consequences.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> There has been some debate surrounding the rhetoric used by the Sexual Offences Review Team. Roffee discusses how the language used manipulates the reader to deem consensual familial sexual acts as not only illegal, but also immoral.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> In Northern Ireland similar offences are against the Sexual Offences (Northern Ireland) Order 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Scotland the offence is against the Criminal Law (Consolidation) (Scotland) Act 1995,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> the provisions of which effectively replaced the Incest and Related Offences (Scotland) Act 1986<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> (although the 1986 Act was not actually repealed until 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Prior to the 1986 Act the law was based on the Incest Act 1567 which incorporated into Scots criminal law Chapter 18 of the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Leviticus" title="Book of Leviticus">Book of Leviticus</a>, using the version of the text of the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Bible" title="Geneva Bible">Geneva Bible</a> of 1562.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> In January 2016 a petition calling for "Adult Consensual Incest" to be decriminalised was submitted to the Scottish Parliament's Public Petitions Committee, but the petition was not debated and no change was made to the law.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marriage_Act_1961_(Australia)" title="Marriage Act 1961 (Australia)">federal marriage law</a> prohibits marriage between an ancestor and descendant or siblings (including a sibling of half-blood), including those traced through adoption.<sup id="cite_ref-MarrAct_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarrAct-118">[118]</a></sup> Also, under federal law, sexual conduct between consenting adults (18 years of age or older) is legal,<sup id="cite_ref-act1994_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-act1994-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> which also applies to close family members. Subject to this overriding federal law, incest continues in the statute books as a crime in every <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">Australian jurisdiction</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> but definitions and penalties vary. </p>
      <p>In all jurisdictions except <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, incest is sexual intercourse between a lineal ancestor and a lineal descendant. In New South Wales, incest takes place between "close family members", which are "parent, son, daughter, sibling (including a half-brother or half-sister), grandparent or grandchild, being such a family member from birth".<sup id="cite_ref-NSWAct_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSWAct-122">[122]</a></sup> Incest generally only applies in cases where a participant is aged 16 or over (the age of consent in that state); and where the participant is aged between 10 and 16 years of age an older participant would generally be charged with sexual intercourse with a child under the age of 16, while cases in which a participant is under 10 an older participant would generally be charged with sexual intercourse with a child under the age of 10. </p>
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, unlawful incest includes sexual intercourse between an uncle or aunt with their niece or nephew, although here its application is curtailed by the effect of the federal <i>Marriage Act</i> 1961, as the Queensland Criminal Code states that the crime of incest does not apply to "persons who are lawfully married or entitled to be lawfully married". Thus it is not incest for a niece aged 16 or over to engage in sexual intercourse with their uncles and a nephew aged 16 or over may engage in sexual intercourse with their aunts. The same principles apply in a same-sex context, as the <i>Marriage Act</i> allows <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>. </p>
      <p>In all other jurisdictions, incest can also arise where one of the parties is below the age of consent, but this does not exclude the possibility of bringing the more general charge of sexual intercourse with a child under the age of 10 (New South Wales and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a>), 12, 16 or 17 (<a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>) as the case may be. This is particularly relevant where a certain form of sexual conduct between related persons falls outside of the legal definition of incest in a particular jurisdiction. </p>
      <p>In no Australian <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">state or territory</a> is consent a defense to incest. The maximum penalty for incest varies: 8 years' imprisonment in New South Wales;<sup id="cite_ref-NSWAct_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSWAct-122">[122]</a></sup> 10 years' imprisonment in South Australia; 20 years' imprisonment in <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Capital_Territory" title="Australian Capital Territory">Australian Capital Territory</a>; 25 years' imprisonment in the Northern Territory, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a>, and Tasmania; and life imprisonment in Queensland. After one conviction for incest, the offender's name is placed on the <a href="/wiki/Sex_offender_registry" title="Sex offender registry">sex offender registry</a> for 15 years, while any offender with two or more convictions for incest has their name placed on the registry for the remainder of their life. </p>
      <p>No particular laws apply to relationships arising from a <a href="/wiki/Sperm_donation" title="Sperm donation">sperm donation</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, incest is sexual connection between a parent and child (both biological and adopted), grandparent and grandchild (both biological and adopted), and full and half-siblings. </p>
      <p>It is a defence if the person was unaware of the relationship at the time of the act (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Accidental_incest" title="Accidental incest">accidental incest</a>). A conviction for incest attracts a maximum penalty of 10 years' imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Incest is the only sexual crime punishable by 7 years or more imprisonment that is not subject to the country's "three-strikes" law.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It is also illegal in New Zealand to have a sexual connection with a dependent child under 18; this includes step-children, foster children and <a href="/wiki/Ward_(law)" title="Ward (law)">wards</a>. A conviction for having a sexual connection, or attempting to have a sexual connection, with a dependent child attracts a maximum penalty of 7 years' imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legality_of_incest&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

        <li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">

      <ul>
       <li>Hughes, Graham.
